  8. I purchased this razor about 2 weeks ago because of the great price and fairly good recommendations from other users. The whole experience soured me a bit on Amazon's customer service. As for the razor, I am very pleased with it overall. I have been using a Norelco 5000 series for a number of years and was never crazy about it. Too much irritation, especially on the neck. And the shave quality went down with the battery charge, with shave time increasing. Maybe that's better with their newer razors due to better technology, I don't know. The Braun gives a very close shave, and absolutely NO irritation at all. The neck is tougher to do, as it was with the Norelco, but I found that you have to turn the razor a bit as you are shaving as the neck hairs must grow at different angles. This gives me a close shave on the neck too. Battery life is great in my opinion, and the razor's speed doesn't seem to slow much as the battery discharges. Quick recharge too. Two disadvantages: the Norelco was easier for me to hold than the Braun, and the Braun does drop stubble while shaving. So shave before putting on the clean white dress shirt!! Since I very rarely use a blade to shave, I can't offer an opinion on the closeness of shave vs a blade. I don't think its a fair comparison anyway. Bottom line, the Braun is significantly better than my old Norleco, and you can't beat the price. I'm happy with my purchase!

The Syncro is far quieter than the buzzy, loud Remington, and eventually does a noticeably better job of getting all the whiskers. <br />Since I shave right after getting out of the shower in the morning I've never noticed whether the unit retains cut whiskers, and don't care. For the record, it doesn't seem to suffer from drop out of cut whiskers. And the units do look brand new - not a scratch on them, gleaming and perfect, at least the two I got.<br />On the negative side, I went through two of these reconditioned units trying to find one which would recharge properly. An old Remington cheapie I've used for a couple of years has recharged perfectly off the same bathroom socket I'm using, and continues to do so without trouble. <br />There seems to be some problem with the provided power cord which causes the recharging function to abort shortly after being plugged in, resulting in almost no recharging. Perhaps when you get the full product with the provided cleaning unit and recharger the unit recharges more reliably, or at least is kept recharged enough so that this problem doesn't show up. <br />I did get the recharging function to work by jiggling the power plug so that it was halfway out of the socket, but what kind of a fix is that? and would it last in the long run? I didn't care to try and have given up on these reconditioned units. Could problems of this sort be why these reconditioned units are so much in evidence both on Amazon and EBay? <br />Braun has discontinued the Syncro line worldwide, except for North America, in favor of a new line it calls the Activator line, its new 8500 series. It has a new type of shaving screen and perhaps an improved recharging system.

It cannot turn itself on during travel. Former Brauns had all sort of tricks to circumvent that problem.<br /><br />Overall:<br />Being a refurbished - and impeccably clean - model, with a full two-year warranty, the price is Ok for a shaver with German technology and a Chinese plug.<br />Paying full price for a brand new model, even with the added (useless) charger / cleaner unit would have had me disappointed.<br /><br />Let's see how long this one lasts. On my former Braun shavers these units lasted 24+ months or more.<br />Question: is the foil/cutter block a minor quality?<br />Luckily I had ordered a spare foil-cutter unit so I could replace it inmediately.   54. Hi. I personally have the model below this, which mainly is the same unit without the charge light and with less advanced charging technology. He really enjoys it, especially after a string of cheap disappointments. I have owned it for a few years and really like it. I also own the charging base which is nice, but not essential. It wasnt always this way, however. When I first started to use it, I didnt get a very good shave with it, despite long shaving sessions, and my chin and jawbone remained hairy despite my best efforts. This being my first electric, I relunctantly settled on the decision that this is how electrics work. They dont give you even close to the shave of a blade, miss lots of hairs, and must be popular mainly for the convenience. I read on Amazon that someone with my same small face and angular jawline had difficulty at first getting an acceptable shave and that for some people the skin of the face builds up a tough epidermal layer to protect from the harshness of the shaver (and probably the harsh alcohol based after shave too). I continued on with my electric shaving, endured comments from female friends like \\"you need to shave\\" only hours after I indeed did, and got used to the limits of my new electric friend. After about a month and a half, things started to change. I started to get a better and better shave, and now a handful of years later I get a great shave with it. Granted its still not as close as a blade, and its easier to miss spots so you really need to check yourself out and see if got everything, but I wouldnt go back to a blade (my face is softer and thanks me!) and I don't think you will either. It's easier, cleaner, more portable, and better on my face, too. I think that can be said about all electrics, but this one does a great job once you \\"break it in\\"- or break your face in, as itmay be. I still use a razor about once a week to clean up my neck, but thats it. Craftsmanship is very high, with low tolerances on the way pieces fit together and a feel of high quality materials throughout. The unit has a nice weight to it that makes it feel solid and well screwed together. Because of this I have purchased a few other Braun products, and found similar levels of quality and engineering in those items, too. IF you're not familar with Braun products, this is a nice introduction to their line of home consumer products. Braun often partners with Gillette, maybe they are owned by them (I'm not sure who is with who anymore!) They are a german company whose products in my experience, are well designed and constructed. Yes, Gillette was notorious for there extensive use of animals in cruel and often unnecessary lab tests, but they have, as a result of public outcry and consumer pressure, halted the development of any new tests and are currently developing non-animal methods. Conscientious buyers (parden the spelling) can now feel less guilty if they are considering this or any Gillette product, at least for now. Gillette recently announced they are being bought by Proctor and Gamble, whose product testing practices are just as dirty and underhanded as the old Gillette ones. TIme will tell how Gillette will fair and whether they will revert back to the outdated, old school ways, but for now... shave on! I realize these comments are about a different model but they both are nearly identical when it comes to shaving dynamics, balance, and cutting ability so comments on its performance can be applied to multiple models that may be under your consideration. This is a great price on this unit too. I'm confident that razors costing twice as much as this one, new or refurb, will not give you the satisfaction of this one. As far as the vendor (Amazon) is concerned, they shipped it out quick and it was received well packaged and charged too. I would rate thebuying process as high as the razor itself. I hope this has been hopeful in deciding if an electric is for you, and if Braun and Amazon are the brand and store you want to get it from! Enjoy and God bless! Happy shaving!

  118. I've been a long time rotary shaver user, mostly Norelcos. I had test drove a few straight blade electrics over the years, but always preferred my current rotary. However I had heard such great things about the Braun electric razors, that I figured I just had to give one a try.<br /><br />This razor does cut close and smooth, and if you have used similiar style razors in the past, you will probably like it. But if you are use to a rotary electric shaver -- beware. I gave the Braun a fair trail of about a month, and while it did a good job, it just takes too dang long to use it. I found that to get a good shave, particularly on my neck and chin, I had to be very careful to run the razor in just the right direction, broadside against the grain, to get good results. Now for you guys who regularly use this type of razor, or a manual razor, you're probably saying, \\"Well, duh!\\" But with a rotary the technique used is more like waxing your car, moving the head in circular motions quickly across your beard. This causes the shaver head to move against the beard's grain for at least some portion of the head's travel allowing it to get a good cut. Personally I've found the end result is being able to shave your entire face much more quickly then with a convention razor or an electric like the Braun.<br /><br />Now the Braun did give me a somewhat closer shave compared to my current 5 year old Norelco with the original blades. And I know some people with problem beards don't find that rotaries give them a close enough shave regardless. If that's your situation, this Braun may be a bargain for you.   123. This is a natural evolution of Braun's revered line of synchro-mesh shavers. Prior to using this one, I had 2 Brauns over the last 6 years (ever since I started using electric razors), each one better than the previous one. This one didn't disappoint either. The shave is closer and more comfortable than the older models. The battery lasts for about a half-hour of shaving (which is about 7-10 shaves), which is standard, or maybe a slight improvement over the older ones. The thing I noticed about the 7526 is that when it runs out of juice, there is no warning -- it just dies (all the other shavers I used ran a little sluggishly for a couple of shaves before dying out). I don't know if it's a good thing or a bad, but my feeling is that the shaver runs at maximum throughput for as long as it can, without ever going sluggish, and then just dies. Which is a good thing... I think. Maybe other reviewers can shed some light on this aspect as well. <br />In terms of the shave, the razor is capable of grabbing almost everything from the face, including finer hair strands in the first attempt, which is a definite improvement. The shave is very close and comfortable. I don't really know how well the adjustable head works, since I always lock the head while shaving. Speaking of the locked position, kudos to Braun for figuring out this design. In this new design, the chances of the shaver \\"slipping\\" to the adjustable position (as with all previous ones) are slim -- gotta love that. Even in the locked position, it works well over contours and corners of the face. The third position is the trimmer, which is pretty effective and does not stick out in an awkward angle like my older 5416 -- another improvement. <br />The \\"refurb\\" package, which I am writing about, comes with a pouch, a cleaning brush and a bulky charger. I wonder why the charger (which was only a cord in the previous editions) actually *grew* in size. It's only a minor irritation, though, and if it's doing the unit anygood, it's an annoyance that can be forgiven. <br />Bottom line, if you can get a shaver like this for this price, just buy it.

  214. I purchased one of these a few months ago and have been completely satisfied. <br /> <br />Of course, shaver performance is very subjective: those who love rotary head shavers often hate foil heads and vice-versa; some think there's nothing like a blade for a good shave, while others find a blade irritating beyond endurance. <br /> <br />Personally, I have been a satisfied user of foil-type electric shavers for years (yes, I've tried other types also). I've found that Braun shavers give me a good shave and are well-made, dependable units. This 7526 unit is no exception. It gives me the closest shave, without irritation, of any shaver that I've ever used. It's quiet (for an electric shaver), and goes for weeks on a single charge. <br /> <br />One particularly nice thing is that this shaver uses an NimH battery, which is not only environmentally friedlier than the older NiCad type, but also should last a lot longer. (NiCad batteries lose their ability to accept a full charge over time, especially if charged before they are completely discharged. Eventually they won't charge at all. Experience with NiMH batteries has shown that they last a *lot* longer and can be charged pretty much whenever you want with no ill effects.) <br /> <br />In addition, the egonomics of the shaver are excellent -- it's well-balanced and comfortable in the hand, and it's easy to see what you are doing even while shaving tricky areas. The off-on switch is designed very well, has very positive action, and should last longer than the design used on earlier Braun shavers. <br /> <br />All in all, I would be happy with the 7526 at full price. At this price for a refurbished unit -- and I couldn't see any sign of previous use at all -- it's a steal.

  298. One of the primary advantages of Amazon reader reviews is that reading several of them about the same product may give a potential buyer a cross section of user opinion and experience about a prospective purchase. This can be especially helpful with a tool such as the factory reconditioned Braun 7526. That's because all beards are not created equal. Skin sensitivity varies. Hairs grow in different directions. Some beards are coarser than others. Because of such differences, the same shaver design that works well for one individual may not give such good results for another person. So, here's my individual user report to add to the general Braun database. <br /> <br />On balance, the Braun does the job for me. In fact, I've put away my safety razor. The Braun is slower to use than that conventional razor, but, if I take the time, it gives me a close shave. I can also now spend shaving time in front of a computer screen or a TV, rather than devoting myself exclusively to shaving in a steamy bathroom. <br /> <br />I have some nerve damage in my shaving hand. This influences my razor choice. The movements I need to make to get a clean shave with a safety razor often produce somewhat colorful results. In personal grooming, this is not a good thing. The rehabilitated Braun is also a little clumsy for me to handle; however, it gives good results without nicks, cuts or other errors. The Braun irritates my skin somewhat more than a blade does, but a splash of Old Spice aftershave fixes that. <br />If I were to buy the Braun today, using the experience I now have, I'd opt for a new unit that comes with the liquid cleaning system. This is because it is difficult for me to effectively clean the Braun's cutters with a brush. The overhauled unit does not come with the snazzy cleaning system. <br /> <br />Without products such as the top-end reconditioned-Braun 7526 on the market, those wishing to try electric shaving would be compelled to buy either low-endjunk (which only teaches that you get what you pay for) or to pay a substantial initiation price for a high-quality model. At about fifty bucks, the Braun makes for a good introduction to electric shaving, without breaking the bank. Even if you eventually decide you're a \\"blade man,\\" at worst you've obtained a backup travel shaver. <br />

  301. I used Braun Syncro 7526 (bought refurbished) for a couple of months now. Before, I used Gillette Mach3, and I probably need to tell about both the shaving method and the particular machine. <br /> <br />The shaving system: <br /> <br />As they say in the manual it takes time for your skin/hair to \\"get used\\" to the new shaving method (2 weeks they say: I totally agree). <br />The first 2 weeks I couldn't get a perfect shaving maybe also because the hair near to my neck used to grow parallel to the skin. Because of the way this machine cuts, the hair has to enter the holes of the foil in order to be cut, and for that it's best if it grows as much away of the skin as possible. During the first 2 weeks I still used my Gillette mach3 for making it \\"perfect\\", or actually to remove the solitary hairs Braun couldn't. <br />After 2 weeks it looked as my hair truly got used to the method, and Braun did a perfect shave. <br />Compared to the classical shave, this method shouldn't be done on wet skin and this turns to be an advantage. It's because when the skin is wet it's also swollen, and the hair can not be cut so well. My girlfriend actually confirmed this as she noticed right away that my skin is a lot softer then before, and it stays longer that way. <br /> <br />About this particular machine: <br /> <br />As I didn't use other type of electrical shaver my opinion could be somewhat one sided, but I'll give my observations: <br />-by buying this unit refurbished from Amazon I think you make an excellent deal, but you should note however that you don't get the cleaning base as when you buy the unit new. However getting it for nearly $100 cheaper, and for only about the double price of the foil and cutter block it makes it such a good deal. And don't think your shaver will get dirtier and dirtier because you lack the original cleaning system. You may keep it clean by following the manual instructions, and it's pretty easy procedure. <br />-the battery lasts truly over 1 month worth of shaving, but not after first charge, and as with all the batteries would be the best if you charge it completely and only when it's empty <br />-the machine has also a sideburns/moustache/beard trimmer, a pretty cool and necessary feature <br />-the shaver looks good overall, it's easy to carry with the charger in the provided carrying pouch, and for travellers: it's international power compliant (you would need top buy plug adapters however, but those are cheap and small as you may know). <br /> <br />I'm happy about the decision I made buying the machine, and I highly recommend it. <br />As I've seen a speculation saying that these machines are sold refurbished for a reason, in my opinion the speculation should be that the reason it's the cleaning base. Maybe that went bad for many items, people returned the shaver and that's why they are sold now refurbished and without the cleaning base. Of course, just a speculation.
